Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A: Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign odontogenic tumour of the mandible. It does not cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  B: Dentigerous cyst is an odontogenic cyst that can form around the crown of an unerupted tooth. It does not cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  C: Orbital fracture is a break in one or more of the bones surrounding the eyeball. It does not cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  D: TMJ ankylosis is a condition in which the temporomandibular joint (TMJ) is fused, preventing normal jaw movement. In bilateral cases, it can cause obstructive sleep apnea.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A: Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign, locally aggressive tumor that arises from odontogenic epithelium.
  B: Dentigerous cyst is an odontogenic cyst that arises from the crown of an unerupted tooth.
  C: Orbital fracture occurs when one of the bones surrounding the eye is broken usually due to direct trauma to the orbital region.
  D: Bilateral TMJ (temporomandibular joint) ankylosis is a disorder that causes limitations in the movement of the jaw due to the stiffness or fusion of the jawbone to the skull.
  
Obstructive sleep apnoea is a medical condition that affects breathing during sleep and is not caused by odontogenic cysts or orbital fractures. Bilateral TMJ ankylosis can limit jaw movement, but it does not directly cause obstructive sleep apnoea. Thus, the most likely answer is A.
Action: Answer("A")

  C: Orbital fractures occur when there is a break in one or more of the bones surrounding the eye. While they can cause vision problems, double vision, and swelling, they are not known to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is when the jaw joint becomes fused and causes limited range of motion. This can cause difficulty chewing, talking and can lead to sleep apnea.

  B: 2 in each jaw
  C: 5 in each quadrant
  D: 2 in each quadrant

  B: This is also incorrect. The number of gum pads does not depend on the jaw bones.

  D: This is not correct. There are more than 2 gum pads in each quadrant.

Topic: Medicine
Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Myocardial infarction is a condition where there is a blockage in blood supply to the heart.
  - Lipid profile is a blood test that checks the level of different types of cholesterol and triglycerides in the blood. 
  - HDL (High-density lipoprotein) is considered as the "good" cholesterol, it helps to remove the excess cholesterol from the bloodstream.
  - LDL (Low-density lipoprotein) is considered as the "bad" cholesterol, it can lead to the buildup of cholesterol in the arteries.
  - TG (Triglycerides) are a type of fat found in the blood.
  - Statins and fibrates are two types of drug classes used to lower the lipid levels.
  
Analysis:
  - The patient had a heart attack two weeks back, which means he is at high risk of having another cardiac event.
  - The lipid profile reveals high TG levels along with low HDL levels. This implies that the patient is at high risk of developing CVD (Cardiovascular Disease).
  - Considering the lipid levels and the patient's medical history, combination therapy with statin and fibrate would be preferred as it reduces the triglyceride levels and increases the HDL levels effectively. 
  - Atorvastatin 80 mg is a high dose of statin and is used in patients with very high LDL levels; it is not an appropriate choice in this case as the LDL levels are not very high.
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Patients with a history of myocardial infarction are considered to be at high risk for cardiovascular disease recurrence.
  Lipid profile is a laboratory test that measures the amount of cholesterol and triglycerides in the blood which is a risk factor for cardiovascular disease.
  LDL is the bad cholesterol, while HDL is the good cholesterol.
  Fenofibrate and statins are two classes of lipid-lowering drugs.
  Fenofibrate is preferred in patients with high Triglycerides levels.
  Statins are the mainstay treatment for high LDL.

Analysis:
  The patient has high triglycerides, and low HDL. Thus, combining Rosuvastatin and Fenofibrate is beneficial as they work on different aspects of lipid profile, but statins are the mainstay of treatment for LDL.

Action: Answer("A")  
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  HDL (High-density lipoprotein) is often called as good cholesterol; High levels of HDL cholesterol can indicate a lower risk of heart disease.
  LDL (Low-density lipoprotein) particles make up the majority of the body's cholesterol. High levels of LDL cholesterol can lead to the buildup of cholesterol in the arteries, increasing the risk of heart disease and stroke.
  TG (Triglycerides) are a type of fat (lipid) found in the blood. High levels of triglycerides can contribute to the hardening of the arteries (atherosclerosis) and increase the risk of stroke, heart attack, and heart disease.
  Statins are most effective in reducing LDL levels and can also increase the levels of HDL cholesterol. 

Analysis:
  The patient is post myocardial infarction with high TG levels which indicates the patient has hypertriglyceridemia, which is a risk factor for atherosclerosis, and the patient also has low HDL levels indicating an increased risk for cardiovascular disease. The goal of lipid-lowering therapy is not only to reduce LDL levels but also to decrease triglyceride levels and increase HDL levels.
  Option A which is a combination of Rosuvastatin and Fenofibrate can be used in this case as it can provide several benefits, including reducing LDL cholesterol, increasing HDL cholesterol levels, and decreasing triglyceride levels.
  Option B with Fenofibrate alone may not be the best choice in this case as it is primarily indicated for hypertriglyceridemia.
  Option C and D using only statins may not target the raised triglyceride cholesterol levels in the patients lipid profile and increase in high HDL levels, but they only reduce LDL levels.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  HDL: High-density lipoprotein (HDL) cholesterol is considered “good” cholesterol because it helps remove LDL (bad) cholesterol from the bloodstream.
  LDL: Low-density lipoprotein (LDL) cholesterol is considered “bad” cholesterol because it contributes to plaque buildup in the arteries.
  TG: Triglycerides (TG) are a type of fat found in your blood.
  Statins are a class of drugs often prescribed by doctors to help lower cholesterol levels in the blood.
  Fenofibrate is a medication used to treat high levels of cholesterol and triglycerides in the blood.

- Fenofibrate alone is mainly used in treating elevations in TG levels.
- Atorvastatin 80 mg dose is often prescribed for high-risk patients to achieve lower LDL levels.

### Exam: medmcqa-dev-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 4 of 100 ###
Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Knowledge:
The third ventricle is a narrow cavity located within the brain, it communicates with the lateral ventricles through the interventricular foramen, and with the fourth ventricle through the cerebral aqueduct. The following structures are present on the floor of the third ventricle:
  A: Optic stalk, also called optic nerve.
  B: Third nerve, also known as oculomotor nerve.
  C: Infundibulum, a funnel-shaped structure that connects the pituitary gland to the hypothalamus.
  D: Mammillary body, a pair of small round structures located in the posterior hypothalamus.

Answer:
  A, B, C are present structures on the floor of third ventricle.
  D is not one of the structures present on the floor of third ventricle.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
The floor of the third ventricle is located in the center of the brain. It is inferior to the thalamus and hypothalamus and is surrounded by other structures like the cerebral peduncles, mammillary bodies, and posterior perforated substance.
  A: The optic stalks are located posterior to the optic chiasm and they form part of the floor and wall of the third ventricle.
  B: Cranial nerve III (oculomotor nerve), which controls eye movement among other functions, emerges from the anterior aspect of the mesencephalon (midbrain) and runs through the lateral wall of the third ventricle.
  C: The infundibulum is a funnel-shaped structure that connects the pituitary gland to the base of the brain. It is located inferior to the hypothalamus and forms part of the floor of the third ventricle.
  D: The mammillary bodies are a pair of small spherical nuclei located on the undersurface of the brain. They are located posteriorly and inferiorly to the floor of the third ventricle.
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The third ventricle is a cavity filled with cerebrospinal fluid (CSF) located in the midline of the brain below the corpus callosum. 
  The floor of the third ventricle is formed by several important structures such as the optic chiasm, infundibulum, mammillary bodies, and the pituitary gland. 
  A: Optic stalk is a structure that connects the optic vesicle with the diencephalon during early embryonic development and it is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  B: The third nerve (oculomotor nerve) arises from the midbrain and lies on the floor of the third ventricle.
  C: Infundibulum is a funnel-shaped structure that connects the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland and it is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  D: Mammillary bodies are two small round structures located on the floor of the diencephalon, posterior to the tuber cinereum, and are part of the limbic system, they are present on the floor of the third ventricle.
Action: Answer("None of the above")

  D: The mammillary bodies are a pair of small round structures located on the underside of the brain, and they are not present on the floor of the third ventricle.
Action: Answer("D")

A: Optic stalk is a part of the optic nerve pathway and connects the optic nerve to the optic chiasm. It is present on the floor of the third ventricle.

Response 6:
Knowledge: 
The third ventricle of the brain is a narrow cavity between the two halves of the thalamus. It is located at the midline of the brain, below the lateral ventricles and above the cerebral aqueduct. Several structures are found on the floor of the third ventricle. 
A: Optic stalk is a structure that connects the eye to the brain and ends in the optic chiasm. It passes through the floor of the third ventricle. 
B: Third nerve is a neurovascular bundle that controls the movement of the eyeball. It exits the midbrain and passes between the posterior cerebral artery and superior cerebellar artery. It runs on the ventral surface of the brainstem and enters the orbit to innervate the eye muscles. It does not pass through the third ventricle. 
C: Infundibulum is a stalk-like structure that connects the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland. It projects downward and lies on the floor of the third ventricle. Its upper end is connected to the hypothalamus, and its lower end enters the pituitary gland. 
D: Mammillary body is a part of the hypothalamus that is involved in memory and spatial navigation. It consists of two small round structures located on the posterior end of the hypothalamus and on the floor of the third ventricle.
Action: Answer("B")

Choices:
  A: Primary hypothyrodism
  B: Pituitary tumor

  D: TSH resistance

  T4 and TSH are thyroid hormones.

  B: A pituitary tumor could cause abnormal levels of various hormones including TSH and growth hormone.
  C: TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma is a rare cause of hyperthyroidism and an excessive secretion of thyroid hormone caused by a pituitary adenoma that produces TSH.
  D: TSH resistance is a rare genetic disorder characterized by a reduced responsiveness of thyrocytes to thyroid-stimulating hormone (TSH).
The description suggests a pediatric patient with low T4 and raised TSH, and swelling of pituitary. This may indicate a pituitary tumor. 
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - T4 is the thyroxine hormone secreted by thyroid and raised TSH indicates an underactive thyroid gland
  - Pituitary gland produces TSH 
  - Swelling of pituitary can lead to various endocrine abnormalities
  
Based on the given information, the most likely diagnosis is that of C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  T4 and TSH hormones are critical for maintaining normal growth, development, and metabolism.
  Primary hypothyroidism is a condition where the thyroid gland fails to produce enough thyroid hormone, leading to elevated TSH levels and decreased levels of T4.
  Pituitary tumors are usually classified based on their hormone-secretion profile and the presence of symptoms, either from excessive hormone release or from local mass effect.
  TSH-secreting pituitary adenomas are rare tumors that secrete abnormally high levels of TSH which leads to secondary hyperthyroidism.
  TSH resistance is a rare disease, in which the TSH receptor fails to respond to TSH, resulting in high TSH levels and low thyroid hormone levels.
  
Action: Answer("C")

  B: A pituitary tumor is a mass or growth that arises from cells in the pituitary gland.
  C: A TSH secreting pituitary adenoma, also known as a thyrotroph adenoma, is a type of pituitary tumor that produces excessive amounts of TSH.
  D: TSH resistance or thyroid hormone resistance is a rare genetic disorder where the thyroid hormone receptor is not able to properly respond to thyroid hormones. This leads to high levels of TSH.

  TSH resistance is a rare genetic disorder in which the thyroid hormone levels are high, but the TSH level is not suppressed, due to resistance to the effects of TSH on the thyroid gland.

Topic: Dental
Question: Pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in
primary teeth because of:
Choices:
  A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young
  B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex
  C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth
  D: Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Pulpectomy is a dental procedure where the pulp tissue inside the tooth is removed, and the canals inside the tooth root are filled with a special material. 
  Pulp capping is a dental procedure where a medicament is placed on the exposed pulp tissue with the aim of protecting the pulp tissue from further injury and encouraging the pulp tissue to heal. 
  Primary teeth typically have more pulp tissue volume than permanent teeth. 
  A: Odontoblasts are cells that form dentin, a layer of tooth tissue below the enamel and cementum. Increased odontoblastic activity can aid in tooth repair. 
  B: Blood supply plays a role in tooth vitality, but a wide apex is not typically associated with primary teeth. 
  C: Primary teeth typically have more pulp tissue volume than permanent teeth. 
  D: Collagen fibres are not typically associated with primary teeth. 
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Pulpectomy is a treatment for removing the entire pulp from the pulp chamber and root canal of a tooth and filling it with an inert material.
  Pulp capping is a treatment to repair and preserve a small area of exposed pulp.
  A: Odontoblast are cells that create dentin. While they are active throughout life, they are more active in primary teeth.
  B: The apex of a primary tooth is wider and allows for more blood supply which is important for healing after these procedures.
  C: The volume of pulp in primary teeth is less than that of permanent teeth.
  D: The amount of collagen fibres in young is not relevant to the success of these procedures.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Pulpectomy is a treatment for infected tooth pulp in which the pulp is removed and the canals of the tooth are cleaned, shaped, and filled.
  Pulp capping is a dental procedure in which a medicament is placed over an exposed tooth pulp to help the pulp regenerate and form new dentin.
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth, also known as baby teeth or deciduous teeth.
  A: Odontoblasts are cells that form dentin, which is the hard, bony tissue that makes up the bulk of a tooth. Increased odontoblastic activity may aid in healing, but it is not specific to primary teeth.
  B: The apex is the tip of the root of a tooth. Increased blood supply may aid in healing, but it is not specific to primary teeth.
  C: The volume of pulp refers to the amount of soft tissue inside a tooth. Primary teeth have less pulp than permanent teeth, so this choice is not correct.
  D: Collagen fibers are a major component of the pulp. Primary teeth have more collagen fibers, which may aid in healing and regeneration, making this the best option.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  Pulpectomy is a dental procedure that involves completely removing the pulp (nerve) from a tooth that is infected.
  Pulp capping is a dental procedure where the exposed pulp is covered (capped) with a medicated material to try to save the tooth. 
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that develop in humans and are also called baby teeth. 
  A: Odontoblasts are cells in the tooth that produce dentin, which is part of the tooth structure that surrounds the pulp. Young children usually have more active odontoblasts which can help in primary tooth repair.

Topic: Pathology
Question: Naive T cell get activated by:
Choices:
  A: NK cell
  B: Dendritic cell
  C: Macrophage
  D: B-lymphocyte
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Naive T cells are T cells that have not yet encountered their target antigen.
  A: NK Cells are natural killer cells that are responsible for identifying and eliminating abnormal cells such as cancer cells and virus-infected cells; they do not activate naive T Cells.
  B: Dendritic cells are professional antigen-presenting cells that activate naive T cells by presenting them with antigen.
  C: Macrophages are also antigen-presenting cells that present antigen to naive T cells to activate them.
  D: B-lymphocytes are responsible for the production and secretion of antibodies in response to antigen exposure, they do not activate naive T cells directly.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: Naive T cells are T cells that have not encountered their specific antigen yet, and hence, are naive to the presence of a particular pathogen. They are activated by antigen-presenting cells (APCs) that display antigen bound to major histocompatibility complex (MHC) molecules on their surface. Dendritic cells are the best APCs at activating naive T cells, due to their superior antigen uptake and presentation capacity. NK cells are part of the innate immune system and are not involved in activating naive T cells. Macrophages can present antigens to T cells, but they are not the most efficient APCs for naive T cell activation. B cells present antigens to helper T cells, but not to naive T cells.

  D: B-lymphocyte plays a role in humoral immunity by recognizing and producing antibodies against specific antigens, but it does not activate naive T cells.

Knowledge: 
  Endolymph has a higher extracellular concentration of potassium ions compared to that in perilymph which is present in the scala vestibuli and scala tympani. Due to the large concentration gradient, potassium ions enter inner hair cells (IHCs) through mechanoelectrical transduction (MET) channels on their stereocilia when the basilar membrane vibrates in response to sound. This generates a receptor potential which is then communicated to the auditory nerve. The potential also depolarizes neighbouring supporting cells and spiral ganglion neurons which make end-to-end synaptic contacts in the spiral ganglion, and spreading the change to the endolymph. This generates the endocochlear potential (EP) between perilymph and endolymph.

Choices:

  B: Lymphatics
  C: Blood vessels
  D: Aspiration of tumor cells
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Metastasis is the spread of cancer cells from one part of the body to another. 
  A: Direct extension is the spread of cancer cells to adjacent tissues.
  B: Lymphatics play a major role in the spread of oral cancer to regional lymph nodes.
  C: Blood vessels enable cancer cells to spread through the body and cause distant metastasis.
  D: Aspiration of tumor cells is associated with a rare but aggressive type of cancer, known as aspiration-associated lung adenocarcinomas.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: Oral cancer is the name given to cancers that develop in the mouth, throat, tongue, or lips. Metastasis is the spread of cancer from the primary site to other parts of the body. 
  A: Direct extension is a type of local spread of cancer and not a route for metastasis.
  B: Lymphatics are often used by cancer cells to spread to nearby lymph nodes and distant organs. Lymphatic spread is a common route of metastasis for many types of oral cancer.
  C: Blood vessels, also known as hematogenous spread, is another route for the metastasis, but it is less common for oral cancer. 
  D: Aspiration of tumor cells is not a recognized route for the metastasis of oral cancer.

A: Direct extension is one of the ways in which cancer can spread. It occurs when a tumor grows into and invades surrounding tissue
B: Lymphatic spread is a common route of metastasis in oral cancer. The oral cavity has a rich lymphatic network that connects it to regional lymph nodes, which are the most common site of oral cancer metastases.
C: Hematogenous spread refers to the spread of cancer cells through the bloodstream. While hematogenous metastasis can occur in oral cancer patients, it is less common than lymphatic spread.
D: Aspiration of tumor cells is not a common route of metastasis for oral cancer.

Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure to treat periodontal disease, also known as gum disease, and involves lifting the gum tissue and cleaning the root surface.
  Root denudation refers to the loss or degradation of the root surface of a tooth.
  PDL fibres (periodontal ligament fibres) are collagen fibres that attach the tooth root to the surrounding bone.
  Cementum is the specialized hard tissue covering the root surface of a tooth.
  Dentin is the hard tissue that forms the bulk of the tooth and surrounds the pulp.
  Epithelium refers to the layer of cells that forms the outer surface of the body.
  In periodontal surgery, co adaptation refers to the process in which the gum tissue reattaches to the surface of the tooth after it has been cleaned.
  
Action: Answer("C") 
During a lateral sliding flap procedure on a tooth with roots that have been denuded for 6 years, it would be expected to see epithelium adjacent to the previously denuded root surface. This is because after the root surface is cleaned, newly formed connective tissue and epithelium will reattach to the root surface. Option A is incorrect because PDL fibres are expected to be lost or degraded in a tooth with long-standing root denudation. Option B is incorrect because PDL fibres are not typically attached to dentin. Option D is incorrect because although co adaptation of the gum tissue to the remaining fibres may occur, it is not relevant to the question.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical dental procedure in which the gingiva is cut and repositioned in order to gain access to the root surface.
  After a tooth has been denuded, the periodontal ligament (PDL) fibers may become detached from its anchorage to the cementum and resorb.
  A: PDL fibers are usually attached to cementum, but if the tooth has been denuded for 6 years, the PDL fibers may have resorbed and detached from the cementum.
  B: PDL fibers will usually not be attached to dentin in normal teeth.
  C: Epithelium may grow over a denuded root surface in the absence of PDL fibers.
  D: Remaining PDL fibers may co-adapt and reorganize in response to changes in the tooth's position or occlusion.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
 A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure for accessing the tooth root.
 Roots denuded for 6 years indicate that the roots of the tooth have been exposed to the oral environment without periodontal attachment for that long of a period.
 PDL fibres are periodontal ligament fibers, which attach tooth roots to the surrounding bone.
Epithelium refers to the tissue that covers the outer surfaces of the teeth and gums.

Answer: 
 The lateral sliding flap would likely reveal epithelium adjacent to the previously denuded root surface and PDL fibers attached to cementum (not to dentin, as they would have typically lost attachment to the denuded dentin surface by this point). Therefore, the best answer choice is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.

  Dentin is the hard, calcified tissue that forms the majority of a tooth's structure.
  Epithelium is a layer of cells that lines the surfaces of the body.

Topic: Gynaecology & Obstetrics
Question: A primigravida came to the labor room at 40 weeks + 5 days gestation for induction of labor. On per vaginal examination, the cervix is 1 cm dilated and 30% effaced. The veex is at --1 station and the cervix is soft and posterior. What will be the modified bishop score for this lady?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 3
  C: 5
  D: 8
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  There are five components of the Bishop Score. 
  The max score for each of the five components is: cervical dilation (3), cervical effacement (2), cervical consistency (1), fetal station (3), and fetal presentation (-5). 
  A higher score indicates the cervix is favorable and is more likely to respond to induction. A Bishop Score of 8 or higher is generally considered to be favorable for induction.
  
  In this case, the patient's cervix is 1 cm dilated (1 point), 30% effaced (0 points), cervical consistency is soft (1 point), fetal station is at -1 station (0 points), and fetal presentation is not mentioned (so we assume it is normal, -5 points). 

Calculation: 
  Bishop Score = cervical dilation + cervical effacement + cervical consistency + fetal station + fetal presentation
  Bishop Score = 1 + 0 + 1 + 0 - 5
  Bishop Score = -3

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

  The bishop score ranges from 0 to 13
  Primigravida means a woman with no previous pregnancies

  Dilatation = 1 cm which gives a score of 0
  Effacement = 30% which gives a score of 0
  Cervical position = posterior which gives a score of 0
  Cervical consistency = soft which gives a score of 1
  Fetal station = -1 which gives a score of 2

Total Score = 0 + 0 + 0 + 1 + 2 = 3

  Each factor is assigned a score from 0 to 2, and the sum of the scores provides an overall modified bishop score ranging from 0 to 8.
  The factors included in the modified bishop score are cervical dilation, cervical effacement, fetal station, and cervical consistency.

  Cervical consistency = not given

  Effacement: 30% = 0 points
  Station: -1= 0 points
  Consistency = not given

  Total = 1

Topic: Dental
Question: Occurrence of malocclusion in given population is best described as:
Choices:
  A: Prevalence rate
  B: Incidence rate
  C: Morbidity
  D: Probability
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Malocclusion refers to misalignment of teeth in the dental arches.
  A: Prevalence rate refers to the proportion of individuals in a population with a specific condition at a given time point.
  B: Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a specific condition that develop in a population during a specific time period.
  C: Morbidity refers to the state of having a specific illness or disease that interferes with normal functioning.
  D: Probability is a measure of the likelihood of an event occurring.
Action: Answer("A") 
Based on the above knowledge, occurrence of malocclusion in a given population is best described as prevalence rate, as it refers to the proportion of individuals in a population with a specific condition at a given time point, which is the best fit to describe the malocclusion in a population.

Knowledge:
  Malocclusion is a misalignment of teeth or incorrect relationship between the teeth of the two dental arches.

Topic: Pharmacology
Question: Digoxin is obtained from a plant product and has a half-life of 36 hours. How does this information help us in formulating treatment?
Choices:
  A: To adjust maintenance dose of digoxin required to keep the blood levels within therapeutic range
  B: Intravenous administration in emergency and urgent dosing
  C: Long half-life permits altemate day dosing
  D: It requires a high loading dose to be administered
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Digoxin is a medication used to treat various heart conditions such as heart failure and atrial fibrillation.
  Digoxin is obtained from the leaves of Digitalis lanata, a plant known as foxglove.
  Half-life is the time taken for the concentration of a drug in the blood to decrease by half.
  Digoxin has a long half-life of 36 hours, which means that it takes a longer time to eliminate from the body.
  A: Adjusting the maintenance dose of digoxin is important as it will help to ensure that the drug's concentration in the blood remains within the therapeutic range.
  B: Intravenous administration is an appropriate route for emergencies, but it is not related to the long half-life of digoxin.
  C: The long half-life indeed permits alternate day dosing, but that is not the only option. 
  D: A higher loading dose may be required in some cases, but this is not always the case.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Digoxin is a cardiac glycoside often used in the treatment of congestive heart failure and atrial fibrillation. It is obtained from the leaves of Digitalis lanata and Digitalis purpurea.
  Digoxin's half-life is 36 hours, which means that it takes 36 hours for half of the dose taken to be eliminated from the body.

Analysis:
  A: The long half-life of digoxin would allow its physician to adjust the maintenance dose necessary to keep blood levels within the therapeutic range.
  B: Intravenous administration in emergency situations refers to the route of administration, and the long half-life does not impact this aspect of administration.
  C: A long half-life permits alternate-day dosing since the drug remains in circulation for an extended period.
  D: The long half-life of digoxin would not require a high loading dose when administering it.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Digoxin is obtained from the foxglove plant and is used to treat heart failure and atrial fibrillation.
  The half-life is the time it takes for half of the dose of a medication to be eliminated from the body.
  A: If a medication has a long half-life, this means that it takes longer for the body to eliminate the medication and therefore it can be dosed less frequently. Knowing the half-life of digoxin can help us adjust the maintenance dose required to achieve and maintain therapeutic blood levels.

Choices:

  B: hysteroscopy
  C: Endometrial biopsy
  D: chromosomal abnormalities

  B: Hysteroscopy is a procedure that allows visual examination of the inside of the uterus. It can be used to identify abnormalities that may have caused previous miscarriages. However, it may not be an appropriate investigation for this scenario.
  C: Endometrial biopsy is a procedure that involves collection of a small sample of the endometrial tissue for examination under a microscope. It may be used to identify any abnormalities that affect the endometrium (the lining of the uterus). However, it may not be an appropriate investigation for this scenario.
  D: Chromosomal abnormalities may cause recurrent miscarriages. Counseling and testing for chromosomal abnormalities (karyotyping) may be appropriate for this scenario.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Preconceptual counseling aims to provide advice and care to women who are planning to conceive, to ensure that they have the healthiest pregnancy possible. 
  A: TVS (Transvaginal ultrasound) may be helpful to check the uterus, ovaries, and the length of the cervical canal.
  B: Hysteroscopy is an invasive procedure in which a thin, lighted tube is inserted into the uterus to check for any structural abnormalities that may cause infertility or miscarriage.
  C: Endometrial biopsy may be performed to assess the tissue lining the uterus for any abnormalities that may prevent pregnancy.
  D: Chromosomal abnormalities can cause recurrent pregnancy loss (RPL).
  
Since the history indicates that the patient has had recurrent second-trimester abortions, it would be wise to investigate the problem before trying to conceive again. The best option among the choices would be to diagnose any structural or functional uterine abnormalities that may be causing the problem. Therefore, I would say that the best course of action is to select choice - B: hysteroscopy.

  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4

  B: Type 2 root canal system has two separate canals joining at some point.

  C: In Dummer's classification, type 3 describes a mandibular molar with three roots and three canals, and has no relevance to apical constriction.

  C: Type 3 describes a root canal system with multiple canals that join into a single canal before exiting the apex of the root.
  D: Type 4 describes a root canal system with multiple canals that exit as separate foramina at the apical end.

ADH acts on the kidneys to increase the reabsorption of water, which reduces urine volume and increases the concentration of the urine.
A: Distal tubules and collecting ducts are the sites where ADH acts by increasing the water permeability of the epithelial cells in the collecting ducts.
B: Afferent arterioles of the glomeruli are not the primary sites of ADH action.
C: The thirst center in the hypothalamus regulates the sensation of thirst, but it is not the primary site of ADH action.
D: Osmoreceptors in the hypothalamus are the primary sites of ADH action. They detect changes in plasma osmolality and trigger the release of ADH to regulate the water balance in the body.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 9:
Knowledge:
 Antidiuretic hormone (ADH) is a hormone that regulates the amount of water reabsorbed by the kidneys.
 A: The distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney are the sites where ADH acts to increase the permeability of the collecting ducts and thus increase water reabsorption.
 B: Afferent arterioles are involved in regulating blood pressure and are not the primary site of action for ADH.
 C: The thirst center in the hypothalamus is stimulated by changes in the osmolality of blood but doesn't directly regulate water reabsorption in the kidneys.
 D: Osmoreceptors in the hypothalamus are the primary site of action of ADH. They sense changes in blood osmolality and stimulate the release of ADH from the posterior pituitary gland to increase water reabsorption in the kidneys.
Action: Answer("D")

Knowledge:
  Jean Piaget's theory of cognitive development outlines four stages of development that children go through.
  A: The sensorimotor stage occurs from birth to about 2 years of age. During this stage, a child's understanding of the world is based on their sensory experiences and actions they perform on objects in the world.
  B: The pre-operational stage occurs from about 2 to 7 years of age. During this stage, children develop language and the use of symbols to represent objects, but still struggle with logical reasoning and understanding that others have different perspectives.
  C: The concrete operations stage occurs from about 7 to 12 years of age. During this stage, children become more adept at logical reasoning and overcoming limitations in their thinking, but only when dealing with concrete objects and events.
  D: The formal operations stage occurs from age 12 to adulthood. During this stage, individuals become capable of abstract reasoning and developing hypotheses, supporting systematic problem-solving skills.
Object Permanence: 
  Object permanence is the understanding that objects continue to exist even when they cannot be seen or heard.

  B: The pre-operational stage occurs from around 2 to 7 years old. During this stage, children improve their language and mental imagery but do not yet comprehend complex concepts such as object permanence.
  C: The concrete operations stage occurs from around 7 to 12 years old. During this stage, children gain an understanding of conservation, reversibility, and cause and effect. They also develop the ability to understand object permanence.
  D: The formal operations stage occurs from around age 12 and through adulthood. This stage is characterized by the development of hypothetical, deductive reasoning, and abstract thinking.

Choices:
  A: Geneva declaration
  B: Helsinki declaration
  C: Hippocratic oath
  D: International code of medical ethics
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A: The Geneva Declaration is a statement of physicians' dedication to the humanitarian goals of medicine that was adopted by the World Medical Association in 1948.
  B: The Helsinki Declaration is a set of ethical principles regarding human experimentation developed for the medical community by the World Medical Association (WMA).
  C: The Hippocratic Oath is an oath of ethics historically taken by physicians.                                              
  D: The International Code of Medical Ethics (ICoME) was adopted by the 3rd General Assembly of the World Medical Association in London in 1949.

Action: Answer("B")  
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The subject matter pertains to principles that govern biomedical research in human subjects. 
  A: Geneva Declaration is a statement that the physician, in general, must not be involved in torture or execution. It is not specifically related to biomedical research.
  B: Helsinki Declaration specifically refers to ethical principles for medical research involving human subjects, and it was adopted by the World Medical Association in 1964. It has been revised several times, the most recent being in 2013.
  C: Hippocratic Oath is an oath that physicians take, promising to uphold specific ethical standards. It is not specific to biomedical research.
  D: International Code of Medical Ethics was adopted by the World Medical Association in 1949 as a declaration of physicians' dedication to the humanitarian goals of medicine. It does not specifically govern biomedical research in human subjects.
Action: Answer("B")

Question: What is the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia?
Choices:
  A: 20 mg
  B: 200 mg
  C: 300 mg
  D: 3000 mg
Response 0:
Knowledge:
Proteinuria is a common feature of pre-eclampsia.
In severe preeclampsia, the degree of proteinuria is usually higher than in mild cases.
A: 20 mg is too low to diagnose severe preeclampsia.
B: 200 mg is also too low to diagnose severe preeclampsia.
C: 300 mg is still too low to diagnose severe preeclampsia.
D: 3000 mg is a very high degree of proteinuria and is commonly used to diagnose severe pre-eclampsia.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Proteinuria refers to the presence of an abnormal amount of protein in the urine. 
  Preeclampsia is a pregnancy complication characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs, often the kidneys.
  Severe preeclampsia is typically defined as meeting any of the following criteria:
    1. Systolic blood pressure ≥160 mm Hg or diastolic blood pressure ≥110 mm Hg on two occasions, at least four hours apart.
    2. Urine protein concentration ≥5 g in a 24-hour urine specimen or ≥3+ protein on two random urine samples collected at least four hours apart.
  Therefore, proteinuria of 5 grams or more in a 24-hour urine specimen is the criteria for severe preeclampsia.
Options:
  A: 20 mg is not significant enough to diagnose severe preeclampsia.
  B: 200 mg is lower than the diagnostic criteria for preeclampsia.
  C: 300 mg is lower than the diagnostic criteria for preeclampsia.
  D: 3000 mg is much higher than the diagnostic criteria for severe preeclampsia.
  
Action: Answer("None of the above")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
- Preeclampsia is a complication of pregnancy characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs, often the kidneys.
- Proteinuria, which is the presence of an abnormal amount of protein in the urine, is one of the diagnostic criteria for preeclampsia. 
- Severe preeclampsia is when there is blood pressure ≥ 160/110 mmHg and proteinuria ≥ 5 g (5000 mg) in a 24-hour urine sample. 
- Therefore, the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia is higher than 3000 mg.

Action: Answer("D")

  Severe preeclampsia is diagnosed when there is proteinuria (greater than or equal to 300 mg in a 24-hour urine collection) in addition to other clinical or laboratory features such as hypertension, thrombocytopenia, impaired liver function, pulmonary edema, or fetal growth restriction.

  C: Chikungunya virus can cause fever, headache, fatigue, nausea, vomiting, myalgia, and rash, but the Tourniquet test is not typically used for diagnosis in patients with Chikungunya.
  D: Swine flu, or influenza A (H1N1) virus, is an influenza virus that causes respiratory illness in people. It does not typically require the use of the Tourniquet test.
Action: Answer("B")

Question: A 9 year old boy presenting with lytic lesion on midshaft tibia. On HPE, there are grooved nuclei, giant cells eosinophilic cytoplasm and fibroblastic proliferation. Xray is as shown below. What is the likely diagnosis?
Choices:
  A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis
  B: Giant cell tumor
  C: Chondroblastoma
  D: Osteoid osteoma
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis can affect bones and presents with lytic lesions. HPE shows Langerhans cells with grooved nuclei and eosinophilic cytoplasm along with histiocytes, multinucleated giant cells and mixed inflammatory infiltrate. 
  B: Giant cell tumor is a benign, locally aggressive tumor that presents with lytic lesions. On HPE it shows predominantly multinucleated giant cells with eosinophilic cytoplasm and pleomorphic nuclei. Fibroblast-like stromal cells are also present.
  C: Chondroblastoma is a benign tumor that is usually located in the epiphysis of long bones. It presents with lytic lesions and on HPE it shows a lobulated appearance with sheets of chondroblasts, cartilage matrix with flocculent calcifications.
  D: Osteoid osteoma is a benign tumor that presents with pain that is worse at night and responds to NSAIDs. It shows a central nidus surrounded by reactive bone formation and is a sclerotic lesion on radiography.

X-ray of the midshaft tibia, as shown below is suggestive of a lytic lesion with soft tissue mass.
 
![tibia-xray](https://aibotanatomy.s3.eu-west-2.amazonaws.com/tibia-xray.png)


Answer: Answer("B") Giant cell tumor
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Langerhans cell histiocytosis is a group of disorders characterized by the abnormal multiplication of certain cells.
  Giant cell tumor is a type of bone tumor, which is frequently found in the knee, but also occurs in the wrist, shoulder, ankle, and other joints.
  Chondroblastoma is an uncommon, benign, cartilage-producing bone tumor.
  Osteoid osteoma is a benign bone tumor that commonly occurs in children and young adults.

Topic: Pediatrics
Question: A neonate presents with jaundice and clay coloured stools. Liver biopsy shows giant cells diagnosis is –
Choices:
  A: Neonatal hepatitis with physiological jaundice
  B: Neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia
  C: Physiological jaundice
  D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Neonate is a term for a newborn baby in the first 28 days of life.
  Jaundice is a common condition in neonates in which bilirubin accumulates in the blood leading to yellow coloured skin and eyes in the baby. 
  Clay-colored stools are a clinical symptom of liver dysfunction.
  A liver biopsy is the removal of a small piece of liver tissue for diagnostic purposes.
  Giant cells are large cells found in inflamed tissues that contain multiple nuclei.

A: Neonatal hepatitis with physiological jaundice is unlikely as clay-colored stools are not a feature of physiological jaundice.
B: Neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia is a possible diagnosis but further investigations are required to confirm the diagnosis.
C: Physiological jaundice is unlikely as clay-colored stools are not a feature of physiological jaundice.
D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia is an unlikely diagnosis as clay-colored stools are not a feature of physiological jaundice.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  1. Jaundice and clay-colored stools indicate liver dysfunction, especially cholestasis.
  2. Giant cells can be seen in neonatal hepatitis, a condition in which the liver becomes inflamed.
  3. Extrahepatic biliary atresia is a congenital disease characterized by the absence or closure of the extrahepatic bile ducts.
  
Analysis:
  1. Physiological jaundice is a common condition in neonates that usually doesn't require treatment and resolves on its own within a few weeks.
  2. Neonatal hepatitis can cause jaundice and liver disease, but the presence of giant cells in liver biopsy suggests a more severe form of liver disease.
  3. Extrahepatic biliary atresia can present with jaundice and clay-colored stools, and often requires surgical intervention soon after birth.

Action: Answer("B") 
The combination of jaundice, clay-colored stools, and giant cells on liver biopsy strongly suggest neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia, which is a serious condition that requires prompt surgical intervention.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
- Neonatal hepatitis is an inflammation of the liver that occurs in the first month of life.
- Jaundice is a yellowing of the skin and whites of the eyes due to an excess of bilirubin, which can occur in neonates as a result of several different conditions.
- Clay-coloured stools are acholic stools and result from a lack of bilirubin excretion into the bile.
- Giant cells are commonly seen on liver biopsy in infants with biliary atresia.
- Extrahepatic biliary atresia (EHBA) is a rare condition in neonates in which biliary ducts are blocked or absent, preventing bile from leaving the liver and causing liver damage.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  1. Neonatal jaundice is common due to the immature nature of the neonatal liver.
  2. Normal conjugation of bilirubin is disturbed in case of neonatal hepatitis.
  3. Biliary atresia is a blockage or absence of the bile ducts that leads to scarring, cirrhosis, and liver failure if not treated.
  
Analysis:
  The neonate is showing symptoms of jaundice and clay colored stools. The presence of giant cells on liver biopsy is suggestive of a hepatitis infection that is causing the liver damage and jaundice. The presence of extrahepatic biliary atresia would cause significant biliary obstruction and not just the typical symptoms observed in neonatal hepatitis or physiological jaundice.

Answer: Answer("B") - Neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia.

Liver biopsy with giant cells may suggest possible diagnoses, such as biliary atresia or hepatitis.

Topic: Biochemistry
Question: In lead poisoning, there is an inhibition of some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway. This is reflected by the accumulation of what substance in blood?
Choices:
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III
  B: Ferrochelatase
  C: Porphob I inogen
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The heme biosynthetic pathway is a multi-step process for the biosynthesis of heme.
  Lead poisoning is known to inhibit enzymes in the pathway leading to accumulation of substrates.
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III is a porphyrin intermediate in the heme biosynthetic pathway, but is not known to accumulate in lead poisoning.
  B: Ferrochelatase is the last enzyme in the pathway which catalyzes the insertion of iron into protoporphyrin IX to form heme. It is not known to accumulate in lead poisoning.
  C: Porphobilinogen is an intermediate that can accumulate in lead poisoning.
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA) is the first committed precursor of heme biosynthesis pathway. Accumulation of ALA in blood or urine is associated with lead poisoning by inhibition of the enzyme delta-ALA dehydratase.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Lead poisoning inhibits some enzymes in the heme biosynthetic pathway, leading to accumulation of porphyrin precursors.
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III is a porphyrin precursor that can accumulate in the blood as a result of inhibition of heme biosynthesis.
  B: Ferrochelatase is an enzyme that catalyzes the insertion of iron into protoporphyrin IX to form heme, and its inhibition would lead to decreased heme synthesis rather than accumulation of porphyrin precursors.
  C: Porphobilinogen is a porphyrin precursor that can accumulate in the urine in some porphyrias, but it is not typically observed in the blood in lead poisoning.
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA) is another porphyrin precursor that can accumulate in the blood as a result of inhibition of the heme biosynthetic pathway, making it the most likely option.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  - Heme biosynthetic pathway involves 8 enzymes that produce heme.
  - Lead poisoning inhibits enzymes 1, 2 and 3 of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  - The inhibition causes an accumulation of the intermediates in the pathway up to the point of the inhibition.
  - Delta aminolevulinic acid (ALA) is the intermediary product of the heme biosynthetic pathway,which accumulates in blood and urine when lead poisoning occurs.
  - Uroporphyrinogen III and porphobinogen III are other intermediaries in the heme biosynthetic pathway
  - Ferrochelatase is the final enzyme in the heme biosynthetic pathway that incorporates iron into protoporphyrin IX to make heme.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  The heme biosynthetic pathway involves 8 enzymes and occurs mainly in the liver and the bone marrow.
  Lead poisoning leads to the inhibition of some enzymes in the heme biosynthetic pathway resulting in the accumulation of some precursors.
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III is a precursor in the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  B: Ferrochelatase is the last enzyme in the heme biosynthetic pathway, and it is involved in the incorporation of iron into protoporphyrin to form heme.
  C: Porphobinogen is a precursor in the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA) is the first precursor in the heme biosynthetic pathway. It is produced from glycine and succinyl-CoA by the enzyme ALA synthase.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 4:
Knowledge: Inhibition of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway can lead to the accumulation of certain intermediate compounds, which normally converted to heme. 
  A. Uroporphyrinogen III can accumulate in patients with porphyrias, which are a group of inherited disorders caused by the deficiency of specific enzymes of heme synthesis.
  B. Ferrochelatase is the last enzyme of the heme biosynthesis pathway that inserts iron into protoporphyrin to form heme. Deficiency of ferrochelatase causes erythropoietic protoporphyria (EPP).
  C. Porphobilinogen is an intermediate compound in the heme synthesis pathway but it is not a substance that accumulates in lead poisoning.
  D. Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA) is an intermediate compound in the heme biosynthetic pathway that can accumulate in cases of lead poisoning.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 5:
Knowledge:
  Lead poisoning inhibits some of the enzymes in the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III is a substrate in heme biosynthetic pathway that is accumulated in porphyria.
  B: Ferrochelatase is an enzyme in heme biosynthetic pathway that incorporates iron into protoporphyrin molecule.
  C: Porphobinogen is an intermediate in heme biosynthetic pathway. It accumulates in porphyria.
  D: Delta-aminolevulinic acid (ALA) is the first intermediate in heme biosynthetic pathway.
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 6:
Knowledge:
  Exposure to lead can interfere with the activity of ALA dehydratase and Ferrochelatase, which are enzymes required for the biosynthesis of heme.
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III is a product of the heme biosynthetic pathway, but it does not accumulate in high levels in lead poisoning.
  B: Ferrochelatase activity is inhibited in lead poisoning, causing the accumulation of a substrate called protoporphyrin IX or free erythrocyte protoporphyrin (FEP) in the blood, and lead-poisoned individuals may have high levels of FEP in their blood.
  C: Porphobilinogen is a precursor of heme that is not increased in lead poisoning.
  D: Delta-aminolevulinic acid (ALA) is a precursor of porphobilinogen that is increased in the blood in lead poisoning because of the inhibition of ALA dehydratase.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 7:
Knowledge:
  Heme biosynthetic pathway involves the synthesis of heme, a vital component of hemoglobin.
  Lead poisoning can cause the inhibition of enzymes involved in the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III is a precursor for the biosynthesis of heme but it is not affected in lead poisoning.
  B: Ferrochelatase is the enzyme that incorporates iron into the heme molecule and is not a substrate for accumulation in case of lead poisoning.
  C: Porphobinogen is a precursor for the biosynthesis of heme and can accumulate in lead poisoning.
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid (Delta-ALA) is the first precursor in the heme biosynthetic pathway and its accumulation occurs in lead poisoning.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 8:
Knowledge:
  Lead poisoning inhibits enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III is an intermediate in the heme biosynthetic pathway that accumulates in congenital erythropoietic porphyria.
  B: Ferrochelatase is the enzyme that inserts iron in the heme molecule.
  C: Porphobilinogen is an intermediate in the heme biosynthetic pathway that accumulates during acute intermittent porphyria.
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA) is an intermediate in the heme biosynthetic pathway and accumulates in lead poisoning.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 9:
Knowledge: 
  Lead poisoning inhibits some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III is an intermediate in the heme biosynthetic pathway, however, an accumulation of this substance is not consistent with an inhibition in this pathway.
  B: Ferrochelatase is the enzyme that forms heme from protoporphyrin IX, therefore, an inhibition of this enzyme may result in the accumulation of protoporphyrin IX in blood.
  C: Porphobinogen is an intermediate in the porphyrin biosynthetic pathway, however, an accumulation of this substance is not consistent with an inhibition in the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA) is the first and rate-limiting step in the heme biosynthetic pathway, therefore an inhibition of this enzyme can result in the accumulation of ALA in blood.
Action: Answer("D")

Topic: Pharmacology
Question: A 70 years old hypeensive patient with stage 5 chronic kidney disease was diagnosed recently with Type 2 diabetes mellitus. He doesn't want to take injectable insulin. Which of the following oral hypoglycemic agents will be preferred in this patient, which won't require any renal dose modification?
Choices:
  A: Linagliptin
  B: Repaglinide
  C: Vildagliptin
  D: Glimepiride
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Patients with stage 5 chronic kidney disease (CKD) have an eGFR less than 15 mL/min and are on dialysis. These patients are at high risk for hypoglycemia because many oral hypoglycemic drugs undergo renal clearance and require dose adjustment.
  A: Linagliptin undergoes hepatic metabolism and is eliminated by biliary and fecal excretion. It does not require dose adjustment in patients with renal or hepatic impairment.
  B: Repaglinide is eliminated via liver and in bile, no renal dose reduction is required.
  C: Vildagliptin is eliminated by renal excretion and its dose need to be reduced in patients with mild to moderate renal impairment. It is contraindicated in severe renal impairment and patients with end-stage renal disease (ESRD)
  D: Glimepiride is extensively metabolized by the liver and excreted predominantly in the urine. It requires dose reduction in patients with moderate to severe renal impairment.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Type 2 diabetes mellitus is a metabolic disorder in which the body becomes resistant to insulin or pancreatic beta cell function decreases. Its management includes changes in lifestyle, diet, and medications if it is required.
  Hypertension and Chronic Kidney Disease are common comorbidities associated with Type 2 diabetes mellitus, especially in older age patients.
  In patients with kidney impairment, the dosages of many oral hypoglycemic agents require adjustments or are contraindicated.
  A: Linagliptin is a dipeptidyl peptidase IV inhibitor used in the treatment of type 2 diabetes. It is eliminated mainly through hepatic metabolism and does not require any renal dose adjustment.
  B: Repaglinide is a meglitinide analog used in the treatment of type 2 diabetes. It undergoes extensive hepatic metabolism and is contraindicated in patients with severe hepatic dysfunction. It is not contraindicated or does not require renal dose adjustment.
  C: Vildagliptin is a dipeptidyl peptidase IV inhibitor used in the treatment of type 2 diabetes. It is hydrolyzed in the liver to inactive metabolites, and no dose adjustment is recommended in patients with mild and moderate renal impairment. However, it is not recommended for patients with severe renal failure.
  D: Glimepiride is a second-generation sulfonylurea used in the treatment of type 2 diabetes. It is contraindicated in patients with severe renal impairment. 
Action: Answer("A")  
Based on the given patient's condition, the preferred oral hypoglycemic agent will be Linagliptin since it doesn't require any renal dose adjustment.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Chronic kidney disease can reduce the elimination and metabolism of oral hypoglycemic agents resulting in their accumulation and toxicity. Therefore, the dose of several antidiabetic agents should be adjusted to avoid toxicity according to the level of renal function.
  
  A: Linagliptin is a DPP-4 inhibitor used in the treatment of type 2 diabetes. It is mainly eliminated by the liver, and dose adjustments are not needed in most patients with renal impairment.
  B: Repaglinide is a meglitinide insulin secretagogue used in type 2 diabetes. It is metabolized and eliminated mainly by the liver, so it is not recommended in patients with end-stage renal disease (ESRD).
  C: Vildagliptin is also a DPP-4 inhibitor used in the treatment of type 2 diabetes. Renal impairment can affect its clearance, requiring careful dose titration and reduction.
  D: Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea used to treat type 2 diabetes. Its active metabolites are mainly excreted in the urine, so it should be carefully titrated in patients with renal impairment.
  
Based on the above facts, in patients with stage 5 chronic kidney disease, Linagliptin would be the best choice as there is no need to adjust the dose in renal impairment.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  Stage 5 chronic kidney disease means end-stage renal disease (ESRD) or GFR <15 ml/min. 
  Among the given drugs, linagliptin and vildagliptin are DPP4 inhibitors and are safe to use in CKD (including ESRD) without dose adjustment.
  Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea, mainly eliminated by kidney, hence its dose should be adjusted in renal failure.
  Repaglinide is eliminated through the liver, but its active metabolites are eliminated through the kidney. Thus, it should be used cautiously with renal disease, although no dose adjustment is generally recommended.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 4:
Knowledge:
  1. Injectable insulin is not the only treatment option for diabetes mellitus.
  2. Chronic kidney disease may limit the use of certain hypoglycemic agents due to the risk of further kidney damage.
  A: Linagliptin is a DPP-4 inhibitor and does not require renal dose modification, and may be used in mild renal impairment. It does not have a hypoglycemic effect at normal glucose levels.
  B: Repaglinide is a sulfonylurea and requires dose adjustment in moderate to severe renal impairment. It is also contraindicated in advanced stage renal disease.
  C: Vildagliptin requires dose reduction in moderate to severe renal dysfunction, and is contraindicated in end stage renal disease (ESRD).
  D: Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea and requires dose modification in moderate to severe renal impairment. It also has a higher risk of hypoglycemia compared to linagliptin.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 5:
Knowledge: 
  1. Chronic kidney disease can cause various degrees of renal impairment and can affect the clearance of drugs from the body.
  2. Oral hypoglycemic agents are categorized based on their mechanism of action, whether they depend on the presence or absence of insulin for their mechanism of action, and their potential for hypoglycemia.
  3. One of the oral agents for treating diabetes mellitus, particularly sulfonylureas, may require dose reduction or avoidance in patients with kidney disease due to concerns of accumulating active metabolites and hypoglycemia.
Action: Answer("A")  
Explanation: 
Based on the given information, the patient has stage 5 chronic kidney disease, which implies significant renal impairment. Therefore, it may be wise to avoid medications that require dose adjustment in the presence of renal dysfunction. Of the options given, Linagliptin is the dipeptidyl peptidase-4 (DPP-4) inhibitor that does not require a dose adjustment, even in severe renal impairment. In contrast, the remaining agents (B, C, D) have varying degrees of dependence on kidney function for their excretion, including Repaglinide, a meglitinide with a comparatively shorter elimination half-life, may increase the risk of hypoglycemia in renal impairment.

Knowledge:
  1. Chronic kidney disease (CKD) can impair the renal excretion of drugs. Therefore, in case of renal impairment, dosage adjustment may be required for some drugs.
  2. Metformin is the first-line agent in most patients with type 2 diabetes mellitus. But in CKD stage 5, it may be contraindicated due to the higher risk of lactic acidosis.

  4. Dipeptidyl peptidase-4 (DPP-4) inhibitors such as linagliptin and vildagliptin are not renally excreted, and their dose does not require modification in renal impairment.

Therefore, among the listed choices, linagliptin and vildagliptin will be preferred over glimepiride and repaglinide.

Question: The patients with class II division 1 malocclusion have
Choices:
  A: Hypertonic Lower Lip
  B: Hypotonic Lower lip
  C: Hypertonic upper Lip
  D: Hypotonic upper lip
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Class II division 1 malocclusion is a type of malocclusion in which the upper front teeth are positioned too far forward or the lower front teeth are positioned too far back, resulting in an excessive overbite.
  A: A hypertonic lower lip can be seen in some patients with class III malocclusion.
  B: Patients with class II division 1 malocclusion often have a hypotonic lower lip. This can contribute to an excessive display of the lower anterior teeth and a gummy smile.
  C: A hypertonic upper lip can be seen in some patients with class II malocclusion as a compensatory mechanism for the excessive overbite.
  D: A hypotonic upper lip is not typically seen in patients with class II division 1 malocclusion.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
- Class II Division 1 malocclusion is a dental classification where the top front teeth (i.e. maxillary central incisors) are located more forward relative to the bottom front teeth (i.e. mandibular central incisors).
- Hypertonic refers to excessive muscle tone or tension.
- Hypotonic refers to reduced muscle tone or tension.

Action: Answer("B") 
Patients with Class II Division 1 malocclusion often have a hypotonic or reduced muscle tone in the lower lip.
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  Malocclusion is a misalignment of teeth and jaws. 
  Class II malocclusion refers to an overbite, which means that the upper teeth and jaw are positioned further forward than the lower teeth and jaw.
  Division 1 malocclusion refers to an overbite in which the upper front teeth are protruded forward compared to the lower front teeth.
  Hypertonic means overly tight or tense muscles, while hypotonic means overly relaxed muscles.

The patients with class II division 1 malocclusion have hypertonic lower lip.

B: Hypotonic lower lip refers to having less than normal tone in the muscles of the lower lip, which is not associated with the class II division 1 malocclusion.
C: Hypertonic upper lip refers to an abnormally high level of tension in the muscles of the upper lip, which may be present in patients with class II division 1 malocclusion.
D: Hypotonic upper lip refers to having less than normal tone in the muscles of the upper lip, which is not associated with the class II division 1 malocclusion.

### Exam: medmcqa-dev-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 85 of 100 ###
Topic: Dental
Question: Resolution of IOPA radiograph is?
Choices:
  A: 16 lp
  B: 22 lp
  C: 30 lp
  D: 10 lp
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  IOPA radiograph (Intra-oral Periapical Radiograph) is a type of dental radiograph that shows the tooth and surrounding structures in detail.
  lp (line pairs) is the unit used to describe the resolution of dental radiographs. The higher the lp, the better the resolution of the radiograph.
  Generally, for intra-oral radiographs, the minimum resolution required is around 20 lp.
  
A and B are close to the minimum resolution required, while D is too low. 
C exceeds what is typically required for intra-oral radiographs.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  IOPA radiograph (Intra-oral periapical radiograph) are used to examine the root apex and surrounding bone. The image produced is high-resolution.
  lp stands for Line pairs
  A line pair is a pair of lines that are separated by a defined distance and varying contrast.
  Hence, lp is a unit of resolution measuring optical density.
  
  The resolution of IOPA radiograph is higher than other radiographs as it requires high resolution for better examination of root apex and surrounding bone.
  
  Higher resolution in dental radiographs comes at the cost of higher radiation exposure, hence care should be taken to minimize exposure, while maintaining an optimal resolution.
  
  A: 16 lp is a lower resolution and not suitable for IOPA radiographs.

  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Knowledge:
- Systematic random sampling is a type of probability sampling in which every nth unit in a list is selected.
- Simple random sampling is a type of probability sampling where each individual in the population has an equal chance of being selected.
- Stratified random sampling is a type of probability sampling where the population is divided into meaningful subgroups (strata) and random samples are taken from each stratum. 
- Cluster sampling is a type of sampling in which random samples are taken from naturally occurring clusters (such as households or schools).
 
Action: Answer("C") 

Stratified random sampling is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results. It is particularly useful when there are known subgroups (such as age groups) in the population and you want to ensure that each subgroup is adequately represented in the sample. By dividing the population into strata, the variability within each stratum is reduced, increasing the precision of the estimates.

Choices:
  A: Give cell culture derived vaccine
  B: Withhold vaccine and observe dog for 10 days
  C: Kill dog and send brain for biopsy
  D: No fuher action is necessary
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Dog bites can be serious because of risk of rabies infection.
  A: Cell culture derived vaccine is a post-exposure prophylaxis for rabies and is usually given to individuals with category II bites, but unnecessary if it was a provoked bite.
  B: Observing the dog for 10 days only applies to individuals who are bitten by a healthy dog with a known owner. 
  C: Killing the dog and sending the brain for biopsy is not necessary if the dog is healthy and observed for 10 days or if it is not available. 
  D: Not taking any action is not appropriate management for unprovoked dog bites.
Action: Answer("A")

Knowledge:
  Dog bites can potentially transmit the rabies virus from the infected dog to the bitten human.
  In case of an unprovoked dog bite, it is important to take appropriate preventive measures to avoid acquiring the disease.
  A: Cell culture-derived vaccine IS recommended to be given immediately after a dog bite if an immunization record doesn't exist. It is also effective post-bite treatment if administered promptly and correctly. 
  B: Observing the dog is not the appropriate action after an unprovoked dog bite. It's important to take prompt action to avoid acquiring the disease.
  C: Killing the dog to be able to send its brain for biopsy is not recommended as it's important to take steps to protect the patient immediately after the dog bite and there are other ways of examining the dog for rabies.
  D: No further action is not accurate as prompt action is required in case of an unprovoked dog bite.

  A: Cell culture-derived vaccine is one of the rabies vaccines that can be administered in case of a dog bite.

The majority of domestic dogs do not have rabies; however, an asymptomatic dog can still transmit the virus to a human during its incubation period. A dog should be observed only if the bite is provoked, and the dog is apparently healthy, and there is adequate assurance of its observation.

  D: Administration of post-exposure prophylaxis (PEP) within hours of exposure following appropriate wound management is necessary in the case of dog bites and rabies exposure. 
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
- The appropriate action for a 10-year boy with a dog bite depends on the nature of the dog.
- Rabies is a serious condition that can be transmitted to humans by the saliva of infected animals.
- The incubation period of rabies in humans can range from a few days to several years, but once clinical signs occur, the disease is almost always fatal.
- The appropriate action for someone bitten by an animal suspected of having rabies is to receive a post-exposure prophylaxis (PEP) as soon as possible after the bite. 
- PEP includes wound cleaning, administration of vaccine and, in some cases, immunoglobulin.
- In the United States, dogs and cats should be observed for 10 days after a bite to determine if they have rabies.

A: Give cell culture derived vaccine - This option is not appropriate as it does not take into account whether or not the dog that bit the boy is infected with rabies. 
B: Withhold vaccine and observe dog for 10 days - This is a reasonable course of action as it allows for observation of the dog to determine if it has rabies. If the dog remains healthy during the 10-day observation period, PEP can be withheld. If the dog develops signs of rabies during the observation period, PEP should be administered and the dog should be euthanized to determine if it has rabies.
C: Kill dog and send brain for biopsy - This is not necessary if the dog can be observed safely for 10 days.
D: No further action is necessary - This is not appropriate as the boy was bitten by a dog and may be at risk for rabies.

Action: Answer("B")
